Explicitly reports `would_execute=false` and `mutation_performed=false`. Blocked environment produces empty plan. 5 new tests.
- Runner Simulation Fixture Queue (Phase 72C): adds `pcae phase runner-sim-fixture`, `--json`, and `--count N` for generating deterministic simulated queue entries (SIM-001 through SIM-010) for runner planning tests. Entries are in-memory only; the real phase queue is never mutated. Count is clamped to 1-10. 5 new tests.
- Runner Stop-Condition Policy Matrix (Phase 72B): adds `pcae phase runner-policy` and `--json` exposing a documented stop-condition policy matrix for bounded runner behavior. Defines 16 conditions across 4 categories: hard stop (10), recoverable stop (2), advisory warning (3), and continue allowed (1). Task finish partial failure points to `pcae task finish recover`. Git lock issues point to `pcae doctor git-lock`. Human authority is explicitly stated as absolute. 4 new tests.
- Bounded Phase Runner Dry-Run Planner (Phase 72A): adds `pcae phase runner-plan`, `--json`, and `--max-phases N` for planning-only bounded runner computation. Shows planned phases from queue (capped at 3), stop conditions, validation sequence, commit/push sequence, and recovery path including `pcae task finish recover` and `pcae doctor git-lock`. Does not execute queue items, mutate queue, create tasks, or make commits. Empty queue reports no planned phases. Blocked environment reports blockers. 7 new tests.
- Phase Queue Runner Readiness Contract (Phase 71Z): adds `pcae phase runner-readiness` and `--json` for read-only three-tier readiness assessment. Reports `environment_ready` (clean tree, healthy, check passed, no active task, task memory clean), `queue_ready` (queue present and non-empty), and `runner_ready` (both environment and queue ready). Includes blocking reasons, advisory reasons, and full governance state. Does not execute queue items. 5 new tests.
- Autonomy Comparison Run Summary Artifact (Phase 71Y): adds `pcae phase autonomy-summary`, `--json`, and `--save` for read-only governance fact summaries useful for agent autonomy comparisons. Reports phases detected, warning count, latest completed phase, recovery command observations, active task, working tree, health, push status, latest handoff summary, and an agent-neutral note. `--save` persists to `.pcae/autonomy-summaries/latest.json` (auto-gitignored). Missing audit or handoff artifacts are handled gracefully. 5 new tests.
- Git Lock Diagnostic Visibility in Task Finish Failure (Phase 71X): when `pcae task finish --commit` fails during the closure commit with `.git/index.lock` or `Operation not permitted` errors, the output now includes actionable guidance: run `pcae doctor git-lock`, then `pcae task finish recover --dry-run`, then `pcae task finish recover --message "..."`. JSON output includes a `guidance` array with these commands. Normal commit failures without lock/permission errors remain unchanged. 3 new tests.
- Audit Handoff Summary Freshness (Phase 71W): `pcae phase audit-show --json` now includes `current_handoff_summary`, `current_handoff_created_at`, and `handoff_summary_stale` fields. When the latest handoff summary differs from the value captured at audit creation time, `handoff_summary_stale` is `true` and human output distinguishes "at audit" from "current" summaries. Existing `latest_handoff_summary` field preserved for backward compatibility. 4 new tests.
- Strategic Continuity Pointer Refresh (Phase 71V): bootstrap prompt now shows "Latest completed phase: <id>" derived from audit or handoff data. When the latest completed phase differs from the strategic lineage's activated phase, the strategic section is relabeled as "Historical strategic decision" to avoid implying it is the current next phase. Historical lineage remains visible for context. 7 new tests.
- Git Index Lock Permission Diagnostics (Phase 71U): adds `pcae doctor git-lock` and `--json` for read-only diagnosis of `.git/index.lock` issues. Reports whether a lock file exists, whether `.git` and `.git/index` are writable, and classifies the situation as `ok`, `lock_present_stale`, `lock_present_active_process`, or `permission_denied`. Each status includes a reason and suggested next action. No lock files are deleted or created. 5 new tests.
- Audit Commit Pair Classification Flexibility (Phase 71T): phase audit commit-pair recognition now accepts `Document`, `Design`, `Add`, and `Refine` verbs as valid implementation commit prefixes alongside `Implement`. Classification uses phase-id matching: any recognized verb followed by `Phase <id>` is treated as implementation unless the verb is `Complete` (which remains closure-only). Phases with documentation-only or design-only commits (e.g., `Document Phase 71S ...`) are no longer falsely warned as missing implementation commits. Warnings for genuinely missing implementation commits are preserved. 7 new tests.
- Codex Autonomy Comparison Handoff Note (Phase 71S): adds architecture documentation for agent-neutral autonomy comparison under PCAE governance. The note defines comparison criteria for Claude/Codex-style runs, expected end-of-run report fields, and the observed Codex 71Q/71Q.1/71R stop-and-recover behavior. It distinguishes agent governance behavior from the Codex sandbox `.git/index.lock` permission issue and reinforces that PCAE should provide governed recovery paths rather than relying on agent improvisation. Documentation only; no code behavior changes.
- Phase Prompt Queue Round-Trip Validation (Phase 71R): adds read-only `pcae phase prompt-roundtrip-check` and `--json` to validate captured prompt planning continuity without executing prompts or mutating prompt artifacts, queue state, or task contracts. The command checks latest prompt metadata/content, prompt-show loadability, prompt-enqueue dry-run derivation, readable phase queue state, planning-only queue-check boundary, and handoff/bootstrap visibility signals when artifacts exist. Missing prompt reports not ready with reasons. Existing queue entries are reported and never cleared.
- Partial Task Finish Recovery (Phase 71Q.1): adds `pcae task finish recover` with `--dry-run`, `--json`, and `--message`. The command detects the narrow post-failure state where task finish already moved exactly one task from `tasks/active/` to `tasks/done/` and updated `tasks/DONE.md`, but the closure commit failed. Recovery stages and commits only those closure files with `git commit --no-verify`; dry-run reports the plan without mutation; JSON reports task id, title, closure files, commit message, commit hash when committed, recovery status, and refusal reason. It refuses unrelated dirty files, ambiguous multiple transitions, active tasks, clean trees, and mismatched active/done filenames. Normal `pcae task finish --commit`, push behavior, task-memory doctor behavior, prompt handling, and queue behavior are unchanged.
- Phase Prompt Queue Metadata Preservation (Phase 71Q): phase queues now accept mixed legacy string entries and structured entries. `pcae phase prompt-enqueue` persists captured-prompt metadata (`title`, `source_type`, `source_prompt_path`, `source_prompt_created_at`, `created_at`) while manual `phase queue add` keeps writing string entries for backward compatibility. Queue list/check normalize titles for human output and expose metadata in JSON when available. Queue hygiene detects placeholder titles across both entry forms. Queue remains planning-only with no prompt execution or queue execution.
- Phase Prompt Queue Bridge Implementation (Phase 71P): adds `pcae phase prompt-enqueue` for safe planning-only bridge from captured phase prompts to the phase queue per 71O design. Enqueues latest prompt by default; `--file <filename>` enqueues a specific timestamped prompt. `--title` overrides queue item title. `--dry-run` reports without mutation. `--json` includes source path, created_at, title, queue length, and mutation status. Duplicate detection refuses entries already in queue. Missing prompt returns clear error. No prompt execution, no task creation, no queue execution. 10 new tests. Later Phase 71Q preserves source metadata in structured queue entries while keeping 71P string queues compatible.
- Phase Prompt Queue Bridge Design (Phase 71O): design document added to `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`. Defines `pcae phase prompt-enqueue latest|<filename>` command shape for transferring prompt title to phase queue entries. Metadata transfer model: title → queue description, path/created_at → informational source fields, content never transferred. Safety model: enqueue only, dry-run first, no execution, no automatic task creation, duplicate detection, multi-phase warning. Explains interaction with queue list/check, handoff/bootstrap visibility, audit artifacts, and future queue runner. No implementation — design only.
- Phase Prompt Hygiene (Phase 71N): adds `pcae phase prompt-hygiene` and `pcae phase prompt-prune` for managing phase prompt artifacts. `prompt-hygiene` detects placeholder-like prompts matching patterns: "test prompt", "placeholder", "dummy", "next step", "todo" (case-insensitive). `--clear-placeholders --confirm` removes only placeholder artifacts, preserving real prompts. `prompt-prune --keep N` retains newest N timestamped prompt artifacts, pruning older ones. `--dry-run` previews prune candidates. `latest.md`/`latest.json` are never touched by prune. Both commands support `--json`. 10 new tests.
- Phase Prompt Visibility in Bootstrap and Handoff (Phase 71M): handoff artifacts now include `prompt_summary` with `present`, `title`, `created_at`, and `path` fields when a captured phase prompt exists. `handoff-show` displays "Latest prompt:" line when present. Compact bootstrap shows "Latest prompt:" in the bootstrap prompt. `pcae session continuity-check` (human and `--json`) includes prompt presence, title, path, and created_at. No prompt mutation during any read surface. 9 new tests.
- Phase Prompt Show (Phase 71L): adds `pcae phase prompt-show` and `pcae phase prompt-list` for displaying captured phase prompts. `prompt-show` displays the latest captured prompt with title, created timestamp, and content. `prompt-show --json` includes all metadata plus content. Missing prompt returns clear error with nonzero exit. `prompt-list` lists timestamped prompt artifacts with count. Both commands are read-only. 8 new tests.
- Phase Prompt Capture (Phase 71K): adds `pcae phase prompt-capture` for saving phase prompts as local runtime artifacts. Supports `--text`, `--file`, and `--stdin` input sources. Creates timestamped artifact and updates `latest.md` and `latest.json` metadata. Artifacts stored in `.pcae/phase-prompts/` (gitignored). `--json` outputs capture metadata. Capture-only — does not execute prompts or create task contracts. Init template updated. 10 new tests.
- Post-Clear Continuity Validation (Phase 71J): adds `pcae session continuity-check` for read-only validation of post-clear/session-reset continuity state. Reports branch, working tree, health, check, task state, task memory, push mode, handoff artifact presence/status, audit artifact presence/status, phase queue presence/count, issues list, and whether repo is suitable for continuation. `--json` produces structured output. Exit code 0 when suitable, 1 when not. Command is strictly read-only. 9 new tests.
- Autonomy Audit Visibility in Handoff and Bootstrap (Phase 71I): handoff artifacts now include `audit_summary` with `present`, `created_at`, `phases_detected`, `warning_count`, and `healthy_idle` fields when a saved audit exists. `handoff-show` displays audit line when present. Compact bootstrap shows "Last audit:" line with phase count, warnings, and healthy idle status. No audit is generated or mutated during handoff or bootstrap. 8 new tests.
- Autonomy Audit Artifact Persistence (Phase 71H): `pcae phase audit --save` persists structured audit reports to `.pcae/phase-audits/latest.json` and timestamped `audit-<ts>.json`. `pcae phase audit-show` displays the latest saved audit (human and `--json`). Missing audit returns clear error with nonzero exit. Audit artifacts are gitignored. Init template updated. Existing audit behavior unchanged without `--save`. 10 new tests.
- Phase Queue Residue Hygiene (Phase 71G): adds `pcae phase queue hygiene` to detect and optionally clear placeholder/test queue entries. Detects entries matching patterns: "test phase", "next step", "placeholder", "dummy" (case-insensitive). `--json` reports findings and clearable count. `--clear-placeholders --confirm` removes only placeholder entries, preserving real queue entries. Without `--confirm`, clearing is refused. Clean queue reports no issues. 12 new tests.
- Governed Phase Queue Runner Design (Phase 71F): design document added to `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`. Refines Phase 70Z runner proposal with concrete specification leveraging 71C–71E infrastructure (`pcae phase audit`, queue visibility, `pcae phase queue check`). Defines `pcae phase queue run` command shape, governed one-phase-at-a-time execution sequence (16 steps), mandatory stop conditions (15 conditions), queue-run audit artifact shape, and external-agent-driven architecture. No implementation — design only.
- Phase Queue Readiness Check (Phase 71E): adds `pcae phase queue check` for read-only readiness validation before executing queued phases. Checks queue exists and is non-empty, working tree clean, health passes, pcae check passes, no active task, task memory clean, push not blocked. Reports `ready` or `not ready` with specific reasons. `--json` includes all readiness fields. 7 new tests.
- Phase Queue Visibility in Handoff and Bootstrap (Phase 71D): handoff artifacts now include `phase_queue_present`, `phase_queue_count`, and `phase_queue_next` fields. `handoff-show` displays queue status when present, silent when absent. Session bootstrap (both human and compact) surfaces queue state from handoff artifacts. No queue mutation during handoff or bootstrap. 8 new tests.
- Autonomy Batch Audit Report (Phase 71C): adds `pcae phase audit` for read-only audit reports on recent autonomous multi-phase runs. Detects implementation/completion commit pairs from git history, reports commit-pair completeness, current health/check/doctor/push state, latest handoff summary, and whether repo returned to healthy idle. Supports `--last N` (default 8), `--since PHASE_ID`, and `--json`. Warns on missing implementation or completion commits. 10 new tests.
- Push Readiness No-Op Semantics (Phase 71B): `pcae push check --json` now includes `push_blocked`, `push_action_required`, `push_noop`, and `push_reason` fields to distinguish benign no-op (`nothing_to_push`) from actual blocked state. `nothing_to_push` reports `push_blocked=false, push_noop=true`. Blocked state reports `push_blocked=true, push_action_required=true`. Existing `ready` field preserved for backward compatibility. 4 new tests.
- Bootstrap Handoff Freshness (Phase 71A): compact bootstrap now shows "Last handoff:" with summary, timestamp, latest commit, task state, review status, and next action when `.pcae/handoffs/latest.json` exists. The stale `PROJECT_STATUS.md` phase is demoted to "Phase (from PROJECT_STATUS.md):" when a handoff artifact provides newer context. Bootstrap without handoff artifact preserves existing behavior. `build_bootstrap_prompt` gains optional `handoff` parameter. 4 new tests.
- Governed Multi-Phase Runner Design (Phase 70Z): design document added to `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`. Proposes `pcae phase run-queue` with governed one-phase-at-a-time execution, mandatory stop conditions (test failure, health/check failure, scope drift, review enforcement), audit artifacts at `.pcae/phase-runs/`, and external-agent-driven architecture. No implementation — design only.
- Phase Queue Planning Command (Phase 70Y): adds `pcae phase queue add/list/show/clear` for advisory phase queue planning. Queue stored in `.pcae/phase-queue.json` (gitignored). Does not execute queued phases or create task contracts. All subcommands support `--json`. 10 new tests.
- Handoff Artifact Hygiene (Phase 70X): adds `pcae phase handoff-prune` to inspect and prune old timestamped handoff artifacts. `--keep N` specifies how many recent artifacts to retain (default: 20). `--dry-run` reports candidates without deleting. `--json` for machine-readable output. `latest.json` is never deleted. 7 new tests.
- Handoff Bootstrap Consumption (Phase 70W): `pcae session bootstrap` now reads and surfaces the latest handoff artifact from `.pcae/handoffs/latest.json` when available. Human output shows "Last handoff:" section with summary, branch, task state, health, check, push, review, latest commit, and next action. JSON output includes `latest_handoff` field (null when no artifact exists). Compact bootstrap `--json` also includes handoff data. Bootstrap does not mutate handoff artifacts. 6 new tests; existing bootstrap behavior preserved when no handoff exists.
- Handoff Artifact Persistence (Phase 70V): `pcae phase handoff` now persists structured handoff artifacts to `.pcae/handoffs/latest.json` and timestamped files. Artifacts include branch, working tree, task state, health, check, push readiness, lifecycle review, recent commits, and bootstrap command. `pcae phase handoff-show` displays the latest artifact (human and `--json`). Handoff directory is gitignored via `.pcae/.gitignore` and init template. JSON output includes all artifact fields alongside existing handoff data. 12 new tests; existing handoff behavior unchanged.
- Phase Handoff Auto-Summary (Phase 70U): `pcae phase handoff` now works with zero arguments. `--summary` is optional; when omitted, a concrete summary is auto-generated from branch, working tree, active task, health, check, unpushed commits, lifecycle review status, and latest commit. When `--summary` is provided, verbatim behavior is preserved. `--next-agent` defaults to the current lock holder when no `--next-agent` and no `--work-type` are provided. JSON output includes `auto_summary` boolean field. 11 new tests; existing handoff behavior unchanged.
- Policy-Controlled Lifecycle Review Enforcement (Phase 70T): adds `[lifecycle_review] require_approved = true` policy flag to make lifecycle review blocking at push readiness. Default behavior remains advisory. When enabled, `pcae push check` fails for `missing`, `changes_requested`, `informational_only`, `mixed`, and `unknown` review statuses; `approved` and `not_applicable` pass. `pcae push` refuses when policy-required review fails. JSON output includes `lifecycle_review_required`, `lifecycle_review_passed`, and `lifecycle_review_reason` fields. Human output shows `(required, passed)` or `(required, failed)` when enforcement is active. `parse_lifecycle_review_require_approved` added to policy parser. 10 new tests; existing advisory behavior unchanged.
- Lifecycle Automation (70A–70K): governed task lifecycle from creation through push. `pcae task finish --commit` validates, closes, and commits in one step. `pcae push` validates readiness and pushes. `pcae doctor task-memory --fix` repairs task-memory inconsistencies. Healthy idle state recognized when no active task exists with a clean working tree. Structured health status (`healthy_active`, `healthy_idle`, `unhealthy`) replaces string-based checks. Runtime session files (`.pcae/session.json`) are untracked by default.

- Implemented Execution Chain Traceability and Status Layer (Phase 69P): read-only observability over the full APA→ARA→EAR→ERR→ERRA→ECP→EPR→PER→RER artifact chain with zero artifact creation, modification, or deletion. `build_execution_chain_status(root, prompt_id)` walks all nine store layers and derives a single `chain_status` spanning `no_record` through `rolled_back` via `_ect_derive_chain_status`; each call re-reads from disk with no caching. `build_execution_chain_doctor(root, prompt_id=None)` runs five advisory-only diagnostic checks: dangling PER→EPR, dangling EPR→ECP, dangling RER→PER (all `severity="error"`), interrupted PER/RER (`in_progress` with no terminal successor, `severity="warning"`), and partial PER/RER (`severity="warning"`); findings never trigger repair, rollback, or re-execution. CLI surfaces: `pcae exec status --prompt-id <id> [--json]`; `pcae doctor execution-chain [--prompt-id <id>] [--json]`. `pcae approval-store show --prompt-id <id> [--json]` and `pcae approval-store list [--json]` expose APA store (via `lookup_approved_prompt_artifact`/`list_approved_prompt_artifacts`). `pcae authorization-store show --prompt-id <id> [--json]` and `pcae authorization-store list [--prompt-id <id>] [--json]` expose ARA store; `list_authorization_artifacts` extended with optional `prompt_id` filter parameter consistent with the filtering pattern of `list_promotion_reviews`, `list_promotion_execution_records`, `list_rollback_execution_records`. `--prompt-id` optional filter added to `promotion-review list`, `promotion-execution list`, and `rollback-execution list` CLI parsers, delegating to the existing `prompt_id` parameters on those list functions. `_ECT_GOVERNANCE_BOUNDARIES` (14 entries) encodes all mutation vectors as forbidden; static guard AST test confirms none of the six 69P read-only handlers calls any mutating function. Regression tests confirm `build_promotion_execution` and `build_rollback_execution` signatures unchanged; list functions retain prior keyword arguments. Design deviation: `authorization-store show` accepts `--prompt-id` (not `--authorization-id`) because the ARA store is keyed by prompt_id (`{prompt_id}-{ts}.json`) and no lookup-by-authorization_id function exists; documented in COMMANDS.md. `_ECT_PHASE_ID="69P"`. 49 `test_69p_*` tests; 5769 total tests passing.
- Transitioned active task from 69O Promotion Rollback Execution to 69P Execution Chain Traceability and Status Layer; session refreshed and governance continuity revalidated.
- Implemented Promotion Rollback Execution (Phase 69O): introduces RollbackExecutionRecord (RER, `.pcae/rollback-executions/`), the first PCAE artifact whose subject is reversing a root mutation, and `pcae rollback` the first command that does so. Internal identifiers use `_RER_*`/`_rer_*` -- checked against existing `_RREP_*`/`_ROLLBACK_*` design-level rollback-governance constants from earlier phases (50A-50K) before naming, no collision. Rollback is gated on a PromotionExecutionRecord (PER) with `status` in `{"completed", "partial"}` and `rollback_payload_available=True`; without that evidence rollback is refused outright (`per_status_not_eligible`, `rollback_payload_unavailable`) and no RER is created, mirroring how ECP/EPR gate failures in 69M/69N never persist anything. `file_plan` is derived strictly from `PER.file_results` where `outcome="success"` -- never user-specified, never including `already_applied` entries, since those were not written by the PER being rolled back (verified against the real 69N schema via `grep`/direct reads before writing any code, per explicit instruction). `_rer_check_divergence` inverts 69N's per-file hash check: a path whose current root hash matches the PER's `after_hash` is `pending` (still promoted, needs reverting); a path matching `before_hash` is `already_reverted` and is skipped without being re-written or treated as an error -- this is how re-running `pcae rollback` against the same PER resumes a partial rollback and is idempotent, with no `--resume` flag; a path matching neither is a `conflict` that blocks the entire attempt before any file is touched (`status="aborted_divergence"`, `file_results=[]`). For each file actually reverted: `before_exists=True` restores `before_content` (decoded from base64 if binary); `before_exists=False` removes the file -- this single rule correctly handles added/modified/deleted promotion entries uniformly without inspecting `change_type`. RER is created with `status="in_progress"` before the first restore and persisted after every file (same Condition-14-style never-silent principle as 69M/69N), so an interrupted rollback is always a stored, inspectable record; a second `pcae rollback` call against a PER with an `in_progress` RER is refused (`rollback_already_in_progress`). Partial rollback (mid-run write failure after divergence passed clean) is a valid terminal state, not automatically retried. `pcae rollback-execution mark-interrupted --rer-id <id>` transitions `in_progress` to `partial` as pure bookkeeping -- no file writes. `rollback_executed` is the first artifact where this field is dynamically `True` (only when this run actually restored/removed a file; `already_reverted` alone leaves it `False`). There is no mechanism to target an RER for reversal (`build_rollback_execution` takes only `per_id`, never `rer_id`), so rollback-of-rollback is forbidden by construction, not by a runtime check. `--dry-run` runs every gate and the divergence check without writing anything and without persisting an RER. CLI: `pcae rollback --per-id <id> [--dry-run]`, `pcae rollback-execution show/list/mark-interrupted`. Explicitly out of scope: `--override-divergence` consumption, multi-PER batch rollback, automatic rollback, git commit/push. 69N marked completed with successor 69O; 69O added as active in execution_governance_activation track with predecessor 69N; BR-005 current_phase advanced to 69O; capability "Promotion Rollback Execution" added to `_CRI_KNOWN_CAPABILITIES`/`_CI_KNOWN_CAPABILITIES`; `_SRG_CAPABILITY_OBJECTIVE_MAP` gains 71st entry; 69N prompt profiles changed from recommended to historical, 3 prompt profiles registered for 69O (recommended); SLR-69O-001 lineage record added (supersedes SLR-69N-001, decision_basis=roadmap_gap, 10 roadmap_debt entries); strategic lineage tests updated (current=SLR-69O-TEST, record_count=26, added `_valid_69o_record()`); `docs/COMMANDS.md`, `docs/ROADMAP_REGISTRY.md`, `docs/CAPABILITY_INVENTORY.md` regenerated; PROJECT_STATUS.md "Governed Root Mutation Achieved" milestone updated to reflect rollback no longer deferred; 52 new `test_69o_*` tests; 5720 total tests passing; execution_allowed=False always; rollback occurs only through the explicit `pcae rollback` human command.
- Transitioned active task from 69N Write Promotion Execution Design to 69O Promotion Rollback Execution; session refreshed and governance continuity revalidated.
- Implemented Write Promotion Execution (Phase 69N): introduces PromotionExecutionRecord (PER, `.pcae/promotion-executions/`), the first PCAE artifact and `pcae promote` the first command that mutates root. Internal identifiers use `_PXR_*`/`_pxr_*` (not `_PER_*`) to avoid colliding with the pre-existing Phase 45N `_PER_*` "Prompt Execution Readiness" constants discovered and fixed during implementation (`_PER_GOVERNANCE_BOUNDARIES` was being silently shadowed). Promotion is gated on an EPR with `promotion_authorized=True`, never on an ECP alone, via `build_promotion_execution(root, epr_id, dry_run=False)`. `_pxr_check_divergence` performs a per-file, resume-aware, content-hash divergence check (three-way: `pending` when current root hash matches ECP `before_hash`, `already_applied` when it matches `after_hash`, `conflict` otherwise or when the path is missing from the ECP or not `promotion_eligible`); git HEAD divergence alone is advisory only, never blocking. `already_applied` paths are skipped, never re-written, never treated as an error, recorded with `outcome="already_applied"` — this is how re-running `pcae promote` against the same EPR resumes a partial promotion, with no `--resume` flag and no additional authority expansion. Any per-file conflict blocks the entire attempt before any file is touched (`status="aborted_divergence"`); the EPR's `override_divergence` field from 69M is deliberately not consumed. PER is created with `status="in_progress"` and `file_results=[]` before the first file write and persisted after every file (mirrors the Condition 14 mandatory-attempt-never-silent principle from 69M), so an interrupted run is always a stored, inspectable record; a second `pcae promote` call against an EPR with an `in_progress` PER is refused (`promotion_already_in_progress`). Partial promotion (some files written, some failed after divergence passed clean — tested via a path that collides with an existing directory to force a write error) is a valid terminal state, not automatically retried. `pcae promotion-execution mark-interrupted --per-id <id>` transitions `in_progress` to `partial` as pure bookkeeping — no file writes, only valid from `in_progress`. `promotion_executed` is the first dynamic occurrence of a field that was a hardcoded `False` invariant on every prior artifact: `True` only when this run actually wrote a file (`already_applied` alone leaves it `False`). `rollback_payload_available` reports whether every successfully-written file had a captured `before_content`/`before_exists=False`; no rollback execution exists. Binary files are decoded from base64 before writing; deletions use `Path.unlink()`. `--dry-run` runs every gate and the divergence check without writing anything and without persisting a PER. CLI: `pcae promote --epr-id <id> [--dry-run]`, `pcae promotion-execution show/list/mark-interrupted`. Explicitly out of scope: rollback execution, git commit/push, automatic promotion, divergence-override consumption, multi-EPR batch promotion, atomic staged-rename writes (sequential write + incremental PER chosen as the smaller mechanism). 69M marked completed with successor 69N; 69N added as active in execution_governance_activation track with predecessor 69M; BR-005 current_phase advanced to 69N; capability "Write Promotion Execution" added to `_CRI_KNOWN_CAPABILITIES`/`_CI_KNOWN_CAPABILITIES`; `_SRG_CAPABILITY_OBJECTIVE_MAP` gains 70th entry; 69M prompt profiles changed from recommended to historical, 3 prompt profiles registered for 69N (recommended); SLR-69N-001 lineage record added (supersedes SLR-69M-001, decision_basis=roadmap_gap, 10 roadmap_debt entries); strategic lineage tests updated (current=SLR-69N-TEST, record_count=25, added `_valid_69n_record()`); `docs/COMMANDS.md`, `docs/ROADMAP_REGISTRY.md`, `docs/CAPABILITY_INVENTORY.md` regenerated; 60 new `test_69n_*` tests; 5668 total tests passing; execution_allowed=False always; root mutation occurs only through the explicit `pcae promote` human command.
- Transitioned active task from 69M Write Governance Design to 69N Write Promotion Execution Design; session refreshed and governance continuity revalidated.
- Implemented Write Governance Design (Phase 69M): introduces ExecutionChangePackage (ECP, `.pcae/execution-packages/`) and ExecutionPromotionReview (EPR, `.pcae/promotion-reviews/`) closing SLR-69L-004 (ECR captures paths not content). ECP is the canonical evidence artifact for sandbox-produced content: per-file `path`, `change_type`, `before_exists`/`after_exists`, `before_hash`/`after_hash` (SHA-256), `diff` (unified diff via `difflib`), `content`/`before_content` (text or base64 for binary), `binary`, `symlink`, `external_target`, `gitignored`, `promotion_eligible`, `exclusion_reason`; `manifest_hash` over all `after_hash` values; `git_head_diverged`/`git_commit_detected` derived from pre/post git HEAD. Condition 14 is the first post-execution governance condition: Conditions 1-13 are pre-execution (failure sets `execution_occurred=False`); Condition 14 evaluates after execution has already occurred inside the sandbox and cannot retroactively block it — ECP capture is a mandatory, ordering-enforced *attempt* inserted between post_state capture and `_esb_destroy_sandbox` in `invoke_readonly_execution`, but capture *success* is not mandated. Failure is never silent: a placeholder ECP is always stored (`capture_outcome="failed"`, partial `capture_errors`), surfaced as `execution_reviewable=False` on both ECP and ERR, rather than retroactively setting `execution_occurred=False`. A call-site try/except around `_ecp_capture` in `invoke_readonly_execution` provides defense in depth beyond `_ecp_capture`'s own internal try/except, guaranteeing sandbox destruction and ERR creation proceed regardless of ECP outcome (preserves ESB-C-003/004 cleanup guarantees from 69L). Hard exclusions (cannot be overridden by EPR): `.git/` (`git_directory_excluded`), `.pcae/` (`governance_directory_excluded`), external symlinks (`symlink_escape`). Default exclusions: toolchain prefixes (`toolchain_artifact_excluded`), gitignored files via batched `git check-ignore --stdin` (`gitignored`), oversized binaries over 1MB (`binary_size_threshold_exceeded`). `_ECP_GOVERNANCE_BOUNDARIES` includes `condition_14_category="post_execution"`, `post_execution_condition_cannot_retroactively_set_execution_occurred_false=True`, `post_execution_condition_failure_sets_reviewability_flag_not_blocker=True`, `ecp_capture_attempt_is_mandatory=True`, `ecp_capture_success_is_not_mandatory=True`, `automatic_promotion_allowed=False`, `production_containment_ready=False` (unchanged from 69L — observability is not containment). EPR (`build_promotion_review`) records a human's content-level review of a specific ECP, distinct from ERRA (execution-result review, not content review): `human_disposition` (approved/rejected/deferred/escalated/cancelled), partial-path approval (`approved_paths`/`rejected_paths`, `partial_approval` derived, `review_state="partial_approved"` when a proper subset of eligible paths is approved), `promotion_authorized` as a separate explicit flag from disposition (no promotion-execution consumer exists yet), `override_divergence`/`override_divergence_rationale`. EPR creation is blocked when the ECP is missing (`ecp_not_found`) or not `execution_reviewable` (`ecp_not_reviewable`); requesting approval of a non-`promotion_eligible` path is a hard validation error (`ineligible_paths_requested`), not a silent drop. `reviewed_by`/`reviewed_at` required only for terminal dispositions (approved/rejected/cancelled). `_EPR_GOVERNANCE_BOUNDARIES` includes `external_symlinks_not_approvable=True`, `pcae_directory_not_approvable=True`, `git_directory_not_approvable=True`, `automatic_approval_allowed=False`. CLI: `pcae execution-change-package show/list` (read-only — ECP can only be created automatically during sandboxed execution, never standalone, since the sandbox no longer exists by CLI invocation time); `pcae promotion-review create/show/list`. No promotion execution, no rollback execution, no git commit, no git push, no automatic promotion — all explicitly deferred to a future phase (69N). - Completed PCAE Parallel Test Execution Standardization (Phase 48X.T): docs/testing/TEST_EXECUTION.md — 6-section test execution guide covering fast validation mode (`python -m pytest -n auto`, benchmark: 3429 tests in ~64s, ~4× faster than serial), balanced battery mode (`python -m pytest -n 4` or `-n 6`, lower CPU/thermal/fan pressure, better battery life, still faster than serial), release verification mode (`python -m pytest`, serial baseline, detects hidden order assumptions), slow test discovery (`python -m pytest --durations=25`), recommended workflow table (fast/battery/release profiles with full pre-commit commands), and safety notes (xdist safe because parallel count matches serial, test count is integrity signal, flaky/shared-state tests break parallel safety, serial remains the final conservative baseline, worker count affects reproducibility); README.md updated with Test Execution Guide link; CONTRIBUTING.md section 5 updated with reference and link to TEST_EXECUTION.md; whitepaper roadmap row for 48X.T updated from Planned to Complete with guide link; whitepaper section 15 parallel test execution paragraph updated with guide link; governance handbook roadmap row for 48X.T updated to complete with guide link; governance handbook remaining milestones updated to reflect 48X.T complete; no source logic changes; documentation only.

nine-stage lifecycle: request → capability_lookup → agent_selection → execution_request_creation → runtime_adapter → agent_execution → result_capture → consensus → governance; execution request model with nine fields: execution_id, parent_task_id, objective, assigned_agent, required_capabilities, execution_mode, writable_allowed, timeout_seconds, metadata; supported runtimes: codex-local, claude-local, kimi-local; future runtimes: deepseek-local, gemini-local, grok-local, perplexity-local, cloud runtimes; result model with nine fields: execution_id, agent_id, status, started_at, completed_at, artifacts, recommendations, confidence, errors; governance integration: framework may invoke runtimes and collect results; framework may not approve, commit, push, or rollback; all governance external; failure model: unavailable_runtime, timeout, execution_failure, partial_result, cancelled, capability_mismatch; human escalation default; future evolution: 44L Runtime Adapter Integration, 44M Controlled Agent Invocation, 44N Real Multi-Agent Planning, 45A Autonomous Roadmap Generation; `EXECUTION_FRAMEWORK_DESIGN_ADVISORY`, `_EXECUTION_FRAMEWORK_LIFECYCLE`, `_EXECUTION_REQUEST_FIELDS`, `_ADAPTER_CONTRACT_FIELDS`, `_ADAPTER_REQUIRED_OPERATIONS`, `_EXECUTION_SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES`, `_EXECUTION_FUTURE_RUNTIMES`, `_EXECUTION_RESULT_FIELDS`, `_EXECUTION_GOVERNANCE_INTEGRATION`, `_EXECUTION_FAILURE_TYPES`, `_EXECUTION_FRAMEWORK_FUTURE_EVOLUTION`, `build_execution_framework_design` added to `core/agent.py`; - Fixed Registry / Summary Consistency (Phase 44D.2): `pcae capability-registry` now passes the documentation capability catalog (`_DOC_CAPABILITY_CATALOG`) to each agent profile builder, matching the behavior of `capability-discovery` and `capability-validation`; kimi-local's `swarm-coordination` now appears as `confidence: observed, evidence_sources: ["documentation_reference"]` in the registry so that `swarm_capable_agents`, `multi_agent_capable_agents`, and all other normalized summary groups are derived directly from registry capability records rather than from a separate hidden source; codex-local's `subagent-coordination` and `skill-execution`, and claude-local's `subagent-coordination` and `custom-agent-support` are also now present in the registry at `observed` from documentation references; no capability is promoted above `observed` by documentation-only evidence; original capability names are preserved; `build_capability_registry` updated in `core/agent.py` with an expanded docstring explaining the source-of-truth fix; 10 new consistency tests verifying that every agent in each summary group has the backing capability at `observed+` with non-empty evidence sources.

- Added Capability Classification Normalization (Phase 44D.1): `pcae capability-registry`, `pcae capability-discovery`, and `pcae capability-validation` discovery summaries now include four normalized capability group fields — `subagent_capable_agents`, `swarm_capable_agents`, `multi_agent_capable_agents`, and `extensibility_capable_agents`; normalization rules: subagent-coordination → multi_agent_capable, swarm-coordination → multi_agent_capable, custom-agent-support → multi_agent_capable, skill-execution → extensibility_capable; kimi-local's swarm-coordination rolls up into multi_agent_capable_agents so all three installed runtimes appear in the group; codex-local's skill-execution rolls up into extensibility_capable_agents; original capability names and confidence levels are never erased or promoted by normalization; `_MULTI_AGENT_CAPABILITIES`, `_EXTENSIBILITY_CAPABILITIES`, `_has_capability_observed`, `_build_normalized_summary` added to `core/agent.py`; `_build_discovery_summary` updated to embed normalized groups; `build_capability_validation` exposes `normalized_summary` as a top-level JSON key with `normalization_rules` mapping; `_print_capability_registry_data` updated in `commands/agent.py` to display all four groups; `run_capability_validation` human output shows normalized capability groups; 13 new tests.

- Added Capability Validation Framework (Phase 44D): `pcae capability-validation` and `pcae capability-validation --json` define how PCAE promotes discovered capabilities from observed to validated/proven through controlled evidence; four-level confidence lifecycle: unknown → observed → validated → proven; seven validation source types: documentation_reference, cli_discovery, manual_validation, runtime_validation, governed_execution_history, writable_execution_history, adapter_contract; four promotion rules — unknown→observed (evidence_collection via documentation_reference or cli_discovery), observed→validated (successful_controlled_experiment via runtime_validation or manual_validation), validated→proven (successful_governed_production_usage via governed_execution_history or writable_execution_history), proven→proven no-downgrade (proven capabilities cannot be downgraded by documentation-only evidence); per-agent validation candidates for all 7 agents with observed_capabilities, validated_capabilities, proven_capabilities, next_validation_candidates, and recommended_validation_method; Codex/subagent-coordination, Claude/subagent-coordination, Kimi/swarm-coordination all surface as observed→validated candidates; JSON output includes `validation_framework` (lifecycle, lifecycle_descriptions, validation_sources, promotion_rules), `promotion_rules`, `validation_candidates`, and `advisory`; human output shows confidence lifecycle, validation sources, promotion rules with descriptions, per-agent candidates, and advisory; `build_capability_validation`, `CAPABILITY_VALIDATION_ADVISORY`, `CAPABILITY_VALIDATION_LIFECYCLE`, `CAPABILITY_VALIDATION_SOURCES`, `_CAPABILITY_PROMOTION_RULES`, `_promotion_rule_for`, `_recommended_validation_method`, `_build_validation_candidates` added to `core/agent.py`; - Added Multi-Agent Collaboration Design (Phase 44A): `pcae collaboration-design` and `pcae collaboration-design --json` generate a read-only collaboration architecture design; design covers four agent roles (planner, implementer, reviewer, validator) with `may_modify_files` semantics (implementer only), runtime mapping for codex-local/claude-local/kimi-local (all four roles), five collaboration patterns (single-agent, dual-agent, review, validation, full-pipeline), governance rules (file modification authority, review/approval/commit/push sequencing), conflict model (halt on reviewer rejection, validator failure, or scope violation), and future extension notes; JSON output includes `collaboration_design`, `runtime_mapping`, `governance_model`, `conflict_model`, `future_extensions`, and `advisory`; `build_collaboration_design` and `COLLABORATION_DESIGN_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_collaboration_design` added to `commands/agent.py`; `collaboration-design [--json]` wired as a top-level command in `cli.py`; strictly read-only — no agents executed, no files modified, no orchestration performed; advisory: "Multi-agent collaboration design is advisory; no orchestration is performed."; 12 new tests.

- Added Controlled Rollback Push (Phase 43E): `pcae remote rollback push JOB_ID` and `--json` push the rollback commit for an approved and executed rollback; push is gated on five conditions: `rollback_approval_state=="approved"`, `rollback_commit_sha` present on the job, `rollback_status` in `("rolled_back", "already_rolled_back")`, clean working tree, and rollback commit reachable from HEAD via `_check_commit_is_ancestor`; on success, `rollback_pushed_at`, `rollback_push_status="pushed"`, and `rollback_remote_branch` are persisted on the job file; JSON output includes `pushed`, `job_id`, `rollback_commit_sha`, `remote_branch`, `push_status`, `advisory`; human output shows Rollback Push header, rollback approval state, rollback commit SHA, push status, remote branch, and advisory; pending/denied approval, missing rollback commit SHA, invalid rollback status, dirty working tree, and unreachable rollback commit all exit 1 with clear messages; git push timeout exits 1; `already_rolled_back` status is accepted for push (idempotent rollback can still be pushed); no new rollback commit is created; `push_rollback`, `ROLLBACK_PUSH_ADVISORY`, `_ROLLBACK_EXECUTED_STATUSES` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_rollback_push` added to `commands/agent.py`; `push JOB_ID [--json]` subcommand wired under `remote rollback` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Rollback push completed through PCAE governance."; 14 new tests.

- Fixed Rollback Result Consistency (Phase 43D.1): `pcae remote rollback execute JOB_ID` is now idempotent; if `rollback_commit_sha` is already recorded on the job, the command returns `rollback_status="already_rolled_back"` with `rolled_back=true` and `exit_code=0` without running `git revert` again; this eliminates the observed split where the first call reported `rolled_back` but a second call emitted `Rollback failed ... git revert exited 1` (because git revert on an already-reverted commit exits 1); JSON and human outputs now always agree — success reports `rolled_back`, repeated execution reports `already_rolled_back`, failure reports the error; `rollback_commit_sha` is preserved from the first execution and never overwritten; no approval state is mutated; no push, reset, or commit deletion occurs; change is a single early-return guard in `execute_rollback` in `core/agent.py`; 6 new tests covering: second execute returns `already_rolled_back`, SHA preserved, no duplicate `git revert` call, required JSON fields on idempotent return, first success emits no failure message, and human/JSON agreement across both invocations.

- Added Controlled Rollback Execution (Phase 43D): `pcae remote rollback execute JOB_ID` and `--json` execute a governed rollback using `git revert --no-edit <original_commit_sha>` for an approved rollback plan; execution is gated on five conditions: `rollback_approval_state=="approved"`, rollback review eligible, `rollback_mode_recommendation=="revert_commit"`, clean working tree, and original governed commit reachable from HEAD via `git merge-base --is-ancestor`; on success: rollback commit SHA captured via `_capture_git_head`, `rollback_commit_sha`, `rollback_status="rolled_back"`, and `rolled_back_at` persisted on the job file; JSON output includes `rolled_back`, `job_id`, `original_commit_sha`, `rollback_commit_sha`, `rollback_status`, `advisory`; human output prints Rollback Execution header, original/rollback commit SHAs, rollback status, and advisory; pending approval exits 1 with "pending" message; denied approval exits 1 with "denied" message; dirty working tree exits 1 with "dirty" message; commit not reachable from HEAD exits 1 with clear error; `git revert` failure exits 1; never pushes; `_run_git_revert`, `execute_rollback`, `CONTROLLED_ROLLBACK_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_rollback_execute` added to `commands/agent.py`; `execute JOB_ID [--json]` subcommand wired under `remote rollback` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Rollback commit created; no push was performed."; 15 new tests.

- Added Rollback Approval Gate (Phase 43C): `pcae remote rollback approve JOB_ID` and `--json` approve a rollback plan; approval is allowed only when the rollback review is eligible (result artifact exists, `commit_sha` is recorded, and `changed_files` is non-empty); persists `rollback_approval_state="approved"` on the job file; JSON output includes `updated`, `job_id`, `previous_rollback_approval_state`, `new_rollback_approval_state`, `rollback_eligible`, `rollback_mode_recommendation`, `advisory`; `pcae remote rollback deny JOB_ID` and `--json` deny a rollback plan; denial is allowed for any rollback-reviewed job regardless of eligibility; persists `rollback_approval_state="denied"`; same JSON output shape; human output shows job id, previous/new rollback approval state, rollback eligible, rollback mode recommendation, and advisory; ineligible jobs exit 1 on approve with clear "not eligible" error; unknown job IDs exit 1; no rollback execution, no git revert, no git reset, no commit, no push; `approve_rollback`, `deny_rollback`, `ROLLBACK_APPROVAL_ADVISORY`, `_ROLLBACK_APPROVAL_STATES` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_rollback_approve`, `run_remote_rollback_deny` added to `commands/agent.py`; `rollback` subparser group with `approve JOB_ID [--json]` and `deny JOB_ID [--json]` wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Rollback approval updated; no rollback was performed."; 17 new tests; strictly read-only — no git operations, no file modifications.

- Added Rollback Review Artifacts (Phase 43B): `pcae remote rollback-review JOB_ID` and `--json` generate a governed rollback review report for a specific job; reads the persisted job and execution result artifact; report fields: `job_id`, `requested_agent`, `original_commit_sha`, `rollback_mode_recommendation` (`revert_commit` when eligible, `not_applicable` otherwise), `rollback_eligible` (True when artifact exists, `commit_sha` present, and `changed_files` non-empty), `eligibility_notes` (reasons when not eligible), `affected_files`, `rollback_risk_level` (low for docs/tasks, medium for src/tests, high for config/policy/deps, critical for scope violations, unknown when no files), `rollback_approval_required` (always True), `rollback_commit_required` (always True), `rollback_push_required` (always True); unknown job IDs exit 1; human output prints Rollback Review section, affected files, recommendation, eligibility, risk level, and approval guidance; `build_rollback_review` and `ROLLBACK_REVIEW_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_rollback_review` added to `commands/agent.py`; `rollback-review JOB_ID [--json]` wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Rollback review is advisory; no rollback is performed."; 13 new tests; strictly read-only — no files modified, no git operations, no approval mutations.

- Added Governed Rollback Design (Phase 43A): `pcae remote rollback-governance` and `--json` expose a read-only rollback governance design; five sections: `rollback_governance` (eligibility model with required/blocking conditions, rollback artifact field definitions, safety rules), `rollback_modes` (three modes: `revert_commit` preferred/allowed, `restore_files` allowed, `reset_branch` dangerous/not allowed by default with `risk_level="critical"`), `risk_model` (four levels: low docs/tasks, medium src/tests, high config/policy/dependency, critical destructive reset), `approval_model` (rollback_review_required, rollback_approval_required, rollback_commit_separate, rollback_push_separate all true; auto_rollback_allowed false; three approval gates: before_rollback_execution, before_rollback_commit, before_rollback_push), `advisory`; human output prints Rollback Governance Design, Rollback Modes, Safety Rules, Risk Model, and Approval Model sections; `build_rollback_governance`, `ROLLBACK_GOVERNANCE_ADVISORY`, and five private constant dicts added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_rollback_governance` added to `commands/agent.py`; `rollback-governance [--json]` wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Rollback governance is advisory; no rollback is performed."; 10 new tests; strictly read-only — no files modified, no git operations, no agents executed.

- Added Governed Commit Lineage Validation (Phase 42E.1): `pcae remote push JOB_ID` now allows push when the governed commit is an ancestor of HEAD, not only when HEAD exactly equals the governed commit; lineage check uses `git merge-base --is-ancestor <commit_sha> HEAD`; three outcomes: `exact_match` (HEAD == governed commit, no warning), `ancestor` (governed commit reachable from HEAD, warning: "Additional commits exist after the governed commit."), or blocked (`ValueError` when governed commit is not in branch history); `lineage_status` and `warnings` added to both JSON output and the human-readable output (warnings printed as `Warning: ...` lines); `_check_commit_is_ancestor(commit_sha, cwd)` added to `core/agent.py` as an injectable helper; `run_remote_push` updated to render warnings; `test_42e_head_mismatch_blocks_push` updated to patch `_check_commit_is_ancestor` and assert "not in current branch history"; 10 new tests covering: push when HEAD equals commit, push when commit is ancestor, warning in JSON output, warning in human output, block when not in history, `lineage_status` field, `warnings` field, `lineage_status="exact_match"`, `lineage_status="ancestor"`, and no warnings on exact match.

- Added Controlled Push (Phase 42E): `pcae remote push JOB_ID` and `--json` execute a governed git push for an approved, committed job; push is allowed only when a result artifact exists, `change_approval_state == "approved"`, `commit_sha` is recorded on the job, the working tree is clean, and current HEAD matches the governed commit SHA; commit message, remote, and branch are derived from the job and git state; `push_status`, `pushed_at`, and `remote_branch` persisted on the job file after a successful push; JSON output includes `pushed`, `job_id`, `commit_sha`, `remote_branch`, `push_status`, `advisory`; human output shows job id, approval state, commit SHA, push status, remote branch, and advisory; refuses with exit 1 for pending/denied approval, missing governed commit, dirty working tree, HEAD mismatch, or git push failure; never creates commits, never approves changes, never modifies files; `_get_current_branch`, `_get_git_remote`, and `_run_git_push` extracted as injectable helpers for testability; `push_file_changes`, `CONTROLLED_PUSH_ADVISORY`, `_get_current_branch`, `_get_git_remote`, `_run_git_push` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_push` added to `commands/agent.py`; `push JOB_ID [--json]` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Push completed through PCAE governance."; 15 new tests.

- Added Controlled Commit (Phase 42D): `pcae remote commit JOB_ID` and `--json` create a governed git commit for approved file changes; commit is allowed only when a result artifact exists, `changed_files` is non-empty, `scope_validation` passed, `change_approval_state == "approved"`, all expected files are present in the working tree, and no unexpected dirty files exist; commit message format is `PCAE: <job_id>\n\nAgent: <agent_id>\nFiles: <count>`; `commit_sha` and `committed_at` persisted on the job file after commit; JSON output includes `committed`, `job_id`, `commit_sha`, `changed_files`, `push_allowed`, `advisory`; human output shows job id, approval state, changed files, commit SHA, push_allowed, and advisory; refuses with exit 1 and clear error for pending approval, denied approval, scope violation, empty changed_files, missing expected files, unexpected dirty files, or git failure; never pushes, never approves automatically, never modifies files; `_run_git_add` and `_run_git_commit` extracted as injectable helpers for testability; `commit_file_changes`, `CONTROLLED_COMMIT_ADVISORY`, `_run_git_add`, `_run_git_commit` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_commit` added to `commands/agent.py`; `commit JOB_ID [--json]` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Commit created; no push was performed."; 16 new tests.

- Added Human Approval Gate for Changes (Phase 42C): `pcae remote changes approve JOB_ID` and `--json` approve file changes from a result artifact; requires artifact present, non-empty `changed_files`, and passing `scope_validation`; sets `commit_allowed=true`, `push_allowed=false`; `pcae remote changes deny JOB_ID` and `--json` deny changes; requires only artifact present; allowed for any job including scope violations; both commands persist `change_approval_state` (`approved`/`denied`) on the job file; return dict includes `updated`, `job_id`, `previous_change_approval_state`, `new_change_approval_state`, `commit_allowed`, `push_allowed`, `advisory`; `changes` subcommand converted from flat parser to subparser group with `show`, `approve`, `deny` subcommands; `_load_job_and_artifact`, `_write_job`, `approve_file_changes`, `deny_file_changes`, `CHANGE_APPROVAL_ADVISORY`, `_CHANGE_APPROVAL_STATES` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_changes` updated to print usage, `run_remote_changes_show`/`approve`/`deny` added to `commands/agent.py`; `approve`, `deny` subcommands wired under `remote changes` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Change approval updated; no commit or push was performed."; 16 new tests; Phase 42B tests updated from `changes JOB_ID` to `changes show JOB_ID`.

- Added Change Review Artifacts (Phase 42B): `pcae remote changes JOB_ID` and `--json` read persisted job and execution result artifact to generate a governed change review; output includes `job_id`, `requested_agent`, `final_status`, `changed_files`, `scope_validation`, `diff_summary`, `risk_level` (`low` for docs/tasks-only, `medium` for src/tests, `high` for config/policy/CI/dependency files, `critical` for scope violations or protected paths), `approval_required` (always true), `commit_allowed` (true when scope is clean and status is completed), `push_allowed` (always false — push requires separate human approval); missing result artifact returns `risk_level="unknown"` with a clear notes field; unknown job IDs exit 1; human output shows change review summary, changed files, risk level, scope validation, approval guidance, and advisory; `_classify_change_risk`, `build_change_review`, and `CHANGE_REVIEW_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_changes` added to `commands/agent.py`; `changes JOB_ID [--json]` wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Change review is advisory; no commit or push is performed."; 15 new tests.

- Corrected Claude Writable Execution Contract (Phase 42A.3.1): `pcae remote execute JOB_ID --invoke --allow-file-changes` for `claude-local` now uses `claude -p --permission-mode acceptEdits <prompt>` based on manual validation; read-only `--invoke` without `--allow-file-changes` remains `claude -p <prompt>` unchanged; `--permission-mode auto`, `--permission-mode bypassPermissions`, and `--dangerously-skip-permissions` are explicitly not used; `_CLAUDE_PERMISSION_MODE_WRITABLE = "acceptEdits"` constant added to `core/agent.py`; `permission_mode` field (`acceptEdits` for claude-local, `n/a` for codex-local and kimi-local) added to returned result dict, persisted artifact, and human output ("Permission mode:" line); Codex sandbox behavior unchanged; Kimi behavior unchanged; post-execution scope validation remains mandatory; no commit or push performed; `test_421_claude_unaffected_by_file_changes_flag` renamed to `test_421_claude_uses_permission_mode_acceptedits_with_file_changes` and updated to verify the correct command; 10 new tests: read-only command unchanged, writable command uses `acceptEdits`, no dangerous flags (auto/bypassPermissions/dangerously-skip), permission_mode in JSON output, permission_mode in persisted artifact, permission_mode in human output, docs/ modification succeeds, Codex permission_mode=n/a, Kimi permission_mode=n/a.

- Added Kimi Writable Execution Contract Inspection (Phase 42A.4): `pcae remote writable-contract kimi-local` and `--json` inspect and document Kimi's writable execution contract before enabling Kimi file modifications; output reports `agent_id`, `current_invocation_command` (`kimi -p <prompt>`), `known_read_only_behavior` (including evidence that `kimi <prompt>` fails with "too many arguments" and listing known options: `-p/--prompt`, `--output-format`, `--plan`, `-S/--session`, `-C/--continue`), `writable_support_status` (`unknown` — not assumed), `required_flags_if_known` (empty — none confirmed), `dangerous_flags` (`--yolo/-y` and `--auto` — explicitly surfaced as not allowed under PCAE governance), `unknowns` (open questions about governed writable behavior without dangerous flags), `safety_recommendation` (conservative: do not enable Kimi writable mode; --yolo and --auto are dangerous and not allowed), and `advisory`; `build_writable_contract(agent_id)` replaces the agent-specific `build_claude_writable_contract` as the unified entry point (shim preserved for compatibility); `dangerous_flags` field added to both Kimi and Claude contracts (empty list for Claude); human output renders a "Dangerous flags" section when non-empty; unknown agent IDs return error dict and exit 1; Claude contract and behavior are unchanged; Codex behavior is unchanged; command is strictly read-only — no agents executed, no files modified; 11 new tests covering human output (dangerous flags section, --yolo, --auto), JSON keys, writable_support=unknown, required_flags=[], invocation command, dangerous flags content, unknowns, conservative safety recommendation, positional-failure evidence, Kimi/Claude independence, and read-only guarantee.

- Added Claude Writable Execution Contract Inspection (Phase 42A.3): `pcae remote writable-contract claude-local` and `--json` inspect and document Claude's writable execution contract before enabling Claude file modifications; output reports `agent_id`, `current_invocation_command` (`claude -p <prompt>`), `known_read_only_behavior` (list), `writable_support_status` (`unknown` — not assumed), `required_flags_if_known` (empty — none confirmed), `unknowns` (list of open questions about sandbox flags and writable behavior), `safety_recommendation` (conservative: do not enable Claude writable mode until contract is confirmed), and `advisory`; unknown agent IDs return an error dict and exit 1 in both human and JSON output; command is strictly read-only — no agents executed, no files modified, Claude writable mode not enabled, Codex and Kimi behavior unchanged; `build_claude_writable_contract(agent_id)` and `CLAUDE_WRITABLE_CONTRACT_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_writable_contract` added to `commands/agent.py`; `writable-contract AGENT_ID` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; 10 new tests covering human output, JSON top-level keys, writable_support_status=unknown, required_flags_if_known=[], invocation command contains `claude -p`, unknowns list non-empty, conservative safety recommendation, unknown agent error (human and JSON), and read-only guarantee (Claude not executed).

- Fixed Git Change Detection After Writable Execution (Phase 42A.2): two bugs fixed — `_capture_git_changed_files` used `root.root` (AttributeError silently caught, always returning []) instead of `root.path`; `git status --porcelain` without `--untracked-files=all` collapses untracked directories to a single `?? dirname/` entry, hiding individual new files; fix applies both corrections: `cwd=str(root.path)` and `git status --porcelain --untracked-files=all`; renamed-file paths (`old -> new`) now take the destination path only; post-execution untracked files (e.g. `docs/remote-controlled-modification-test.md`) are now correctly detected, scope-validated, and reported as `final_status=completed`; `completed_with_no_changes` now fires only when git truly reports no changes; same `root.root → root.path` fix applied to `_capture_git_head` and `_capture_diff_summary`; integration tests now commit all initial repo files and add `remote/` to `.pcae/.gitignore` so job/result artifacts don't contaminate post-execution change detection; 6 new tests covering: untracked file in tracked dir, untracked file in wholly-untracked dir (regression for the collapse bug), clean tree returns empty, integration docs creation → completed, integration no-agent-writes → completed_with_no_changes, integration src/ write → scope violation.

- Added Codex Writable Sandbox Contract (Phase 42A.1): `pcae remote execute JOB_ID --invoke --allow-file-changes` now uses `codex exec --sandbox workspace-write` for codex-local instead of `--sandbox read-only`; read-only `--invoke` without `--allow-file-changes` continues to use `--sandbox read-only` unchanged; Claude (`claude -p`) and Kimi (`kimi -p`) commands are unaffected by the `--allow-file-changes` flag and receive no sandbox argument; `sandbox_mode` field added to result return dict and persisted result artifact (`workspace-write` for codex-local, `n/a` for other adapters); `sandbox_mode` displayed in human-readable output ("Sandbox mode:" line) and JSON output; `_build_invoke_command` gains `allow_file_changes` parameter (default False); post-execution scope validation and file capture remain mandatory; no commit or push performed; 9 new tests covering codex read-only sandbox unchanged, codex workspace-write selected, sandbox_mode in JSON/artifact/human output, Claude unaffected, Kimi unaffected, docs/ success, src/ violation still detected.

- Added Controlled File Modification (Phase 42A): `pcae remote execute JOB_ID --invoke --allow-file-changes` and `--json` extend the existing execution pipeline with governed file-write capability; pre-execution HEAD SHA captured via `git rev-parse --short HEAD`; changed files captured via `git status --porcelain` after execution; diff summary captured via `git diff --stat`; Phase 42A scope rules allow only `docs/` and `tasks/` modifications and deny `src/`, `tests/`, `.pcae/`, `.git/`, `.github/`, `pyproject.toml`, and policy files; scope violations set `final_status=failed` with per-file violation messages; no changed files sets `final_status=completed_with_no_changes`; agent process failure sets `final_status=failed`; change metadata (`changed_files`, `scope_validation`, `pre_execution_head`, `diff_summary`, `file_changes_allowed=true`) persisted in result artifact; no commit, push, or rollback performed; existing `--invoke` without `--allow-file-changes` remains fully read-only and unchanged; `invoke_remote_job_with_file_changes(root, job_id)`, `_capture_git_head`, `_capture_git_changed_files`, `_capture_diff_summary`, `_validate_file_change_scope` added to `core/agent.py`; `_run_remote_execute_invoke_file_changes` added to `commands/agent.py`; `--allow-file-changes` flag added to `remote execute` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Files may have been modified, but no commit or push was performed."; 15 new tests.

- Added File Modification Governance Design (Phase 41M): `pcae remote file-governance` and `--json` expose a read-only governance design document for future file-modifying autonomous coding; seven design sections: writable_scope_rules (repository root constraint, allowed paths, denied paths, generated artifact paths, protected files), change_capture (changed files, diff collection, modification summary, risk classification), approval_workflow (human_review_required=true, four checkpoints: before_execution/after_execution/before_commit/before_push, rejection handling, re-execution requirements), commit_governance (commit separated from execution, approval requirements, metadata requirements including job ID and agent attribution), push_governance (push separated from commit, branch restrictions, approval requirements), rollback_strategy (prerequisites, artifact requirements, recovery workflow), safety_model (read-only default, file-modifying opt-in, protected operation handling); risk_model defines four levels (low/medium/high/critical) with classification scheme and advisory note; advisory: "This phase defines governance only; no file modifications are performed."; `build_file_governance_design()` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_file_governance` added to `commands/agent.py`; `file-governance` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; 9 new tests; strictly read-only.

- Added Controlled Runtime Benchmarking plan preview (Phase 41L.1): `pcae remote benchmark controlled --dry-run` and `--dry-run --json` preview a controlled benchmark plan without executing agents; plan fields include `runtimes` (claude-local, codex-local, kimi-local), `prompt` (identical across all runtimes), `runs_per_runtime` (3), `execution_mode` (non_interactive), `human_approval_required` (true), `total_planned_runs` (9), and `sandbox_behavior`; `planned_metrics` lists duration_seconds, exit_code, stdout_length, stderr_length, output_classification, success_or_failure; `future_metrics` lists mean_duration, median_duration, p95_duration, stddev_duration, success_rate; `limitations` explicitly labels duration as end-to-end wall-clock time and notes rankings require sufficient data; advisory: "Controlled benchmarks measure end-to-end runtime execution, not pure model performance."; `build_controlled_benchmark_plan()` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_benchmark_controlled` added to `commands/agent.py`; `controlled` subcommand with required `--dry-run` wired under `remote benchmark` in `cli.py`; existing `pcae remote benchmark` historical command unchanged; 9 new tests; strictly read-only — no agents executed, no jobs created, no runtime state mutated.

- Added Runtime Benchmarking (Phase 41L): `pcae remote benchmark` and `--json` compute per-runtime benchmark metrics (`execution_count`, `success_rate`, `average_duration_seconds`, `fastest_execution_seconds`, `slowest_execution_seconds`, `latest_execution`, `output_classification_breakdown`) and global rankings (`fastest_runtime`, `slowest_runtime`, `highest_success_rate`) with `benchmark_confidence` (`insufficient_data`/`low`/`medium`/`high`) based on the minimum per-runtime execution count (thresholds: ≥20=high, ≥10=medium, ≥5=low, <5=insufficient_data); `output_classification_breakdown` counts all four output classes per runtime; rankings are deterministic via alphabetical tie-breaking; malformed artifacts skipped with per-file warnings; JSON output includes `benchmark_summary`, `runtime_metrics`, `rankings`, `warnings`, `advisory`; `build_remote_runtime_benchmark(root)`, `_compute_benchmark_confidence`, and `_BENCHMARK_CONFIDENCE_THRESHOLDS` added to `core/agent.py`; delegates to `build_remote_results_registry`; `run_remote_benchmark` added to `commands/agent.py`; `benchmark` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Runtime benchmarks are computed from persisted execution history."; 11 new tests covering empty, JSON structure, per-runtime metrics, output_classification_breakdown, rankings, insufficient/low confidence thresholds, human output, malformed file warnings, and read-only guarantee.

- Added Execution Trends (Phase 41K): `pcae remote trends` and `--json` compute historical trend metrics from persisted result artifacts; global `trend_summary` includes `total_executions`, `execution_timespan` (seconds between oldest/newest `finished_at`), `trend_status`, `success_rate_trend`, `average_duration_trend`, `oldest_execution`, and `newest_execution`; per-runtime `runtime_trends` includes `execution_count`, `average_duration`, `fastest_execution`, `slowest_execution`, `success_rate` for each agent; trend indicators are `increasing`, `decreasing`, `stable`, `insufficient_data`; fewer than 5 total executions → all indicators `insufficient_data`; ≥5 entries → first-half vs second-half average comparison with 10% relative change threshold for `stable` vs `increasing`/`decreasing`; `trend_status` reflects `success_rate_trend`; malformed artifacts skipped with per-file warnings; `build_remote_execution_trends(root)` and `_compute_trend_indicator` added to `core/agent.py`; delegates to `build_remote_results_registry`; `run_remote_trends` added to `commands/agent.py`; `trends` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Execution trends are computed from persisted execution history."; 10 new tests covering empty, insufficient data, stable with 5 results, JSON structure, runtime breakdown, oldest/newest ordering, malformed file warnings, human output, and read-only guarantee.

- Added Execution Report Inspection (Phase 41J): `pcae remote report inspect REPORT_FILE` and `--json` read an exported report file by path (relative or absolute), validate required field presence, and report `validation_status` (`valid`, `partial`, `invalid`); missing files exit 1 with a clear error; malformed JSON or non-object content returns `validation_status="invalid"` with `report=null` and a warning; partial reports (missing one or more required fields) return `validation_status="partial"` with per-field `"Missing required field: ..."` warnings; required fields: `advisory`, `exported_at`, `failed_executions`, `latest_execution`, `result_registry_summary`, `runtime_breakdown`, `success_rate`, `successful_executions`, `total_executions`; human output shows file, validation status, key metrics, runtime breakdown, latest execution, and optional `report_version`; JSON output includes `report_path`, `validation_status`, `report` (full dict or null), `warnings`, `advisory`; `inspect_remote_execution_report(root, path)` and `REMOTE_REPORT_INSPECT_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_report_inspect` added to `commands/agent.py`; `inspect` subcommand wired under `remote report` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Report inspection is read-only; no agents are executed."; 7 new tests covering valid inspection, JSON output, required fields, missing file, malformed JSON, partial report warnings, and read-only guarantee.

- Added Execution Report Export (Phase 41I): `pcae remote report export` and `--json` generate a governed execution report from persisted result artifacts and write it to `.pcae/remote/reports/remote-execution-report-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS.json`; report content includes `exported_at`, `total_executions`, `successful_executions`, `failed_executions`, `success_rate`, `runtime_breakdown` (per-agent metrics dict), `latest_execution`, `result_registry_summary` (`result_count`, `warnings`), and `advisory`; command JSON output returns `export_path`, `exported_at`, `total_executions`, `success_rate`, `advisory`; human output shows export path, execution count, success rate, and advisory; `report` subcommand uses two-level subparser structure (`remote → report → export`) following the `jobs` pattern; `reports/` is covered by the existing `remote/` entry in `.pcae/.gitignore`; `export_remote_execution_report(root)` and `REMOTE_REPORTS_DIR` added to `core/agent.py`; delegates to `build_remote_execution_analytics` and `build_remote_results_registry`; `run_remote_report_export` added to `commands/agent.py`; `report`/`export` subparsers wired in `cli.py`; advisory: "Execution report export is read-only; no agents are executed."; 7 new tests covering file creation, human output, JSON metadata, report file content, empty registry, result immutability, and filename format.

- Added Execution Analytics (Phase 41H): `pcae remote analytics` and `--json` compute global execution metrics (`total_executions`, `successful_executions`, `failed_executions`, `success_rate`, `average_duration_seconds`, `fastest_execution`, `slowest_execution`, `latest_execution`) and per-runtime metrics (`executions`, `successes`, `failures`, `average_duration`) keyed by `selected_agent`; any runtime appearing in result artifacts is captured automatically; all metrics return `None`/empty gracefully when no results exist; malformed artifacts produce per-file warnings and are skipped; JSON output has `analytics`, `runtime_metrics`, `warnings`, `advisory`; human output shows global summary and runtime breakdown; `build_remote_execution_analytics(root)` and `_compute_runtime_metrics` added to `core/agent.py`; both delegate to `build_remote_results_registry` for file scanning, avoiding duplicated I/O logic; `run_remote_analytics` added to `commands/agent.py`; `analytics` subcommand wired under `remote` in `cli.py`; advisory: "Execution analytics are computed from persisted result artifacts."; 11 new tests; strictly read-only — no agents executed, no results mutated.

- Added Remote Execution Result Registry (Phase 41G): `pcae remote results` (no argument) lists all persisted execution result artifacts from `.pcae/remote/results/`, sorted newest first; each entry reports `job_id`, `selected_agent`, `final_status`, `exit_code`, `duration_seconds`, `output_classification`, `output_path`, and `finished_at`; malformed files produce per-file warnings and are skipped; empty/absent directory returns empty list; `--json` outputs `result_count`, `results`, `warnings`, `advisory`; `pcae remote results JOB_ID` continues to work unchanged; `build_remote_results_registry(root)` and `REMOTE_REGISTRY_ADVISORY` added to `core/agent.py`; `run_remote_results` split into `_run_remote_results_registry` and `_run_remote_results_single`; `job_id` made `nargs="?"` in CLI parser; advisory: "Execution result registry is read-only; no agents are executed."; 9 new tests covering empty registry, JSON structure, result listing, newest-first sort, malformed file warnings, output_classification field, backward-compat job_id path, and read-only guarantee; strictly read-only — no agents executed, no jobs or results mutated.

- Added Execution Output Normalization (Phase 41F): `pcae remote results JOB_ID` and `--json` now include `output_classification` and `normalized_final_output` fields in `execution_result`; four classification values: `clean_stdout` (stdout has content, stderr empty), `stderr_with_status_text` (stderr has content regardless of stdout — covers Kimi's reasoning/status text pattern), `empty_output` (both stdout and stderr are blank), `execution_error` (non-zero exit code); `normalized_final_output` is the stripped stdout string for `clean_stdout` and `stderr_with_status_text` classifications, or `null` for `empty_output` and `execution_error`; raw `stdout` and `stderr` in persisted result artifacts are never modified; `stdout_summary` and `stderr_summary` are preserved unchanged; human output shows "Output classification:" and "Normalized final output:" lines when a result is available; `_classify_execution_output` and `_normalize_final_output` helpers added to `core/agent.py`; four classification constants exported (`OUTPUT_CLASS_CLEAN_STDOUT`, `OUTPUT_CLASS_STDERR_STATUS`, `OUTPUT_CLASS_EMPTY`, `OUTPUT_CLASS_ERROR`); 9 new tests cover Codex clean_stdout, Claude clean_stdout, Kimi stderr_with_status_text, empty output, execution error, JSON field presence, raw artifact preservation, human output display, and Kimi stderr-only normalized_final_output=None; strictly read-only — no job files mutated, no agents executed, no approval state changed.

- Added Multi-Runtime Execution Validation (Phase 41E): no new execution features; validates the full governed execution lifecycle (create → persist → approve → readiness gate → execute → result persistence → result reporting) for both `claude-local` and `kimi-local` using the existing execution framework; 17 new tests organized into four groups — (1) full lifecycle tests for each runtime covering job creation, approval, readiness gate passing, exit_code=0, final_status=completed, artifact persisted, results reporting, and no-commit guarantee; (2) result persistence tests verifying artifact content (job_id, selected_agent, exit_code, final_status, timing fields, full expected stdout) for each runtime; (3) reporting tests verifying JSON and human output of `pcae remote results` for each runtime; (4) adapter selection tests verifying claude-local uses `["claude", "-p", ...]`, kimi-local uses `["kimi", "-p", ...]`, and that the two runtimes use distinct executables; validation prompt is `"Read-only task: reply with exactly:\nPCAE {runtime} execution validation successful.\nDo not modify files."`; no `core/agent.py` or `commands/agent.py` changes; all tests use monkeypatched subprocess and discovery to avoid real agent execution.
